Proceed.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="53" speaker="CORNELIUS">Your daughter, whom she bore in hand to love</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="54" speaker="CORNELIUS">With such integrity, she did confess</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="55" speaker="CORNELIUS">Was as a scorpion to her sight; whose life,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="56" speaker="CORNELIUS">But that her flight prevented it, she had</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="57" speaker="CORNELIUS">Ta'en off by poison.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="58" speaker="CYMBELINE">O most delicate fiend!</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="59" speaker="CYMBELINE">Who is 't can read a woman? Is there more?</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="60" speaker="CORNELIUS">More, sir, and worse. She did confess she had</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="61" speaker="CORNELIUS">For you a mortal mineral; which, being took,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="62" speaker="CORNELIUS">Should by the minute feed on life and lingering</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="63" speaker="CORNELIUS">By inches waste you: in which time she purposed,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="64" speaker="CORNELIUS">By watching, weeping, tendance, kissing, to</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="65" speaker="CORNELIUS">O'ercome you with her show, and in time,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="66" speaker="CORNELIUS">When she had fitted you with her craft, to work</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="67" speaker="CORNELIUS">Her son into the adoption of the crown:</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="68" speaker="CORNELIUS">But, failing of her end by his strange absence,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="69" speaker="CORNELIUS">Grew shameless-desperate; whose containing</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="523" speaker="POSTHUMUS LEONATUS">Is so from sense in hardness, that I can</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="524" speaker="POSTHUMUS LEONATUS">Make no collection of it: let him show</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="525" speaker="POSTHUMUS LEONATUS">His skill in the construction.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="526" speaker="CAIUS LUCIUS">Philarmonus!</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="527" speaker="Soothsayer">Here, my good lord.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="528" speaker="CAIUS LUCIUS">Read, and declare the meaning.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="529" speaker="Soothsayer">[Reads]  'When as a lion's whelp shall, to himself</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="530" speaker="Soothsayer">unknown, without seeking find, and be embraced by a</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="531" speaker="Soothsayer">piece of tender air; then shall Posthumus end</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="535" speaker="Soothsayer">his miseries, Britain be fortunate and flourish in</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="536" speaker="Soothsayer">peace and plenty.'</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="537" speaker="Soothsayer">Thou, Leonatus, art the lion's whelp;</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="538" speaker="Soothsayer">The fit and apt construction of thy name,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="539" speaker="Soothsayer">Being Leonatus, doth import so much.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="540" speaker="Soothsayer">The piece of tender air, thy virtuous daughter,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="541" speaker="Soothsayer">Which we call 'mollis aer;' and 'mollis aer'</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="542" speaker="Soothsayer">We term it 'mulier:' which 'mulier' I divine</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="543" speaker="Soothsayer">Is this most constant wife; who, even now,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="544" speaker="Soothsayer">Answering the letter of the oracle,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="545" speaker="Soothsayer">Unknown to you, unsought, were clipp'd about</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="546" speaker="Soothsayer">With this most tender air.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="547" speaker="CYMBELINE">This hath some seeming.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="548" speaker="Soothsayer">The lofty cedar, royal Cymbeline,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="549" speaker="Soothsayer">Personates thee: and thy lopp'd branches point</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="550" speaker="Soothsayer">Thy two sons forth; And, Caius Lucius,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="556" speaker="CYMBELINE">Although the victor, we submit to Caesar,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="557" speaker="CYMBELINE">And to the Roman empire; promising</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="558" speaker="CYMBELINE">To pay our wonted tribute, from the which</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="559" speaker="CYMBELINE">We were dissuaded by our wicked queen;</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="560" speaker="CYMBELINE">Whom heavens, in justice, both on her and hers,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="561" speaker="CYMBELINE">Have laid most heavy hand.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="562" speaker="Soothsayer">The fingers of the powers above do tune</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="563" speaker="Soothsayer">The harmony of this peace. The vision</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="564" speaker="Soothsayer">Which I made known to Lucius, ere the stroke</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="565" speaker="Soothsayer">Of this yet scarce-cold battle, at this instant</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="566" speaker="Soothsayer">Is full accomplish'd; for the Roman eagle,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="567" speaker="Soothsayer">From south to west on wing soaring aloft,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="568" speaker="Soothsayer">Lessen'd herself, and in the beams o' the sun</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="569" speaker="Soothsayer">So vanish'd: which foreshow'd our princely eagle,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="570" speaker="Soothsayer">The imperial Caesar, should again unite</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="571" speaker="Soothsayer">His favour with the radiant Cymbeline,</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="572" speaker="Soothsayer">Which shines here in the west.</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="573" speaker="CYMBELINE">Laud we the gods;</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="574" speaker="CYMBELINE">And let our crooked smokes climb to their nostrils</line><line act="5" scene="5" line="575" speaker="CYMBELINE">From our blest altars.
